--- Page 16 ---
IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO.       OF 2025
(Arising out of SLP(C) No.16305/2018)
THE EXECUTIVE ENGINEER TAMIL NADU HOUSING BOARD APPELLANT
                         VERSUS
V.N. MOHAMED HUSSAIN (DEAD) THR. LRS. & ORS.    RESPONDENTS
   O R D E R
1. Leave granted.
2. Heard learned counsel for the appellant as well as
learned senior counsel for the respondents.
3. The issue that falls for consideration is whether
the subject acquisition, which was initiated way back on
17.07.1978, is liable to be declared to have lapsed under
Section 24(2) of the Right to Fair Compensation and
Transparency  in  Land  Acquisition,  Rehabilitation  and
Resettlement Act, 2013 (in short, the “2013 Act”). The
High Court has, vide the impugned judgment, held that
neither compensation was paid nor possession of the land
was taken and hence both statutory conditions having been
satisfied, the acquisition has lapsed.
4. During the course of hearing, three questions arise
for consideration:
Firstly,  the  appellant’s  case  is  that  the
respondents are subsequent purchasers, and therefore,
they cannot seek declaration under Section 24(2) of the
1

--- Page 17 ---
2013 Act. On the other hand, the respondents vehemently
contest this issue, and they deny their status as the
subsequent purchasers. This aspect has not been gone into
by the High Court in the impugned judgment.
The Second issue that emerges is whether the Land
Acquisition  Collector  had  taken  possession  of  the
acquired  land,  with  or  without  depositing  the
compensation amount. It seems that a greater clarity is
required to determine this question of fact. Answer to
this is also not discernible from the contents of the
impugned judgment.
Third issue will be that if the State fails to take
physical possession of the land or the compensation was
not paid and if the subject land is still required for
completion/execution of a public project, what should be
the recourse to be followed by the appellant-State?. This
question has been effectively answered by this Court in
somewhat similar circumstances in the case of Tamil Nadu
Housing  Board  &  Anr.  vs.  Poovatha  &  Ors. ,  (C.A.
Nos.13256-13257/2024).
5. In the facts and circumstances noticed above, it
seems to us that the above-stated three questions need to
be effectively determined by the High Court.
6. Consequently, but without expressing any opinion on
the merits, we allow this appeal in part; set aside the
impugned judgment dated 18.08.2017 of the High Court; and
remit  the  case  back  to  the  High  Court  for
2

--- Page 18 ---
re-determination of the questions raised hereinabove or
any such question(s) that may arise for consideration
during the course of hearing. The parties shall be at
liberty to raise their respective contentions and also
file  additional  documents,  if  so  required,  for  the
consideration of the High Court.
7. Having regard to the age of the acquisition, we
request the High Court to accord priority in final
hearing, with an endeavour to decide the matter within a
period of four months. 
8. The parties are directed to maintain status quo re:
creation of third party rights, construction or creating
any encumbrance on the subject property till the matter
is decided by the High Court.
...................CJI.
(SURYA KANT)
.....................J.
(JOYMALYA BAGCHI)
New Delhi
December 08, 2025
3

For Respondent(s) Mr. Balbir Singh, Sr. Adv.
                   Mr. Himanshu Satija, Adv.
                   Mr. Raheel Patel, Adv.
                   Ms. Neha Mehta Satija, AOR
                   Ms. Ripul Swati Kumari, Adv.
                   Mr. Anshul Rao, Adv.   
Mr. Varun Kalra, Adv.
Mr. Nishant Thakur, Adv.
M/s DSK Legal, AOR                             
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1.  Dr. A.M. Singhvi, learned senior counsel for the appellant
assails the National Company Law Appellate Tribunal (NCLAT) order
dated 25.05.2026 on the ground that the resolution plan was
approved by the Committee of Creditors (CoC) in October, 2020 when
the Covid Pandemic was raging. Soon thereafter 90% creditors

--- Page 25 ---
2
including appellant’s assignor resiled from the decision. The NCLT
had  rightly  taken  these  circumstances  into  consideration  and
declined to approve the resolution plan. It is further contended
that the resolution plan merely covers 10% of the admitted debts
and other statutory dues were also not included. He further argues
that the valuation of the assets of the company were incorrectly
made which led NCLT to disallow the plan under Section 31(2) of
IBC, 2016.
2.  In rebuttal, Mr. Balbir Singh, learned senior counsel for the
respondents submitted that the appellant was not a member of the
CoC and that the commercial wisdom of the CoC has already been
approved by this Court in the earlier round of litigation. It is
submitted that the resolution plan had been approved in 2020 and
his clients have furnished necessary guarantees and funds for
implementation of the plan. 
3.  It is true that in the earlier round of litigation, the issue
whether the CoC could revisit its earlier approval had been decided
against them. However, the matter was remitted to NCLT for a fresh
look. NCLT after considering various aspects including inadequate
valuation of the Net Present Value (NPV) (as assessed in 2020
during pandemic period) and refused to approve the resolution plan.
The order has been overturned by NCLAT primarily on the ground that
NCLT has not specifically stated which provision of Section 30 of
the Act was contravened in the plan.
4.  Having gone through the impugned judgment, we are of the
opinion, the following issues, inter alia, fall for consideration:
(i) Whether the NCLT was justified in holding that the resolution

--- Page 26 ---
3
plan failed to comply with requirements under section 31(1) of IBC,
2016?
(ii) Whether the litigation with regard to properties at Neemrana
and Jamdoli was correctly assessed and considered while approving
the resolution plan?
(iii) Whether valuation of NPV in the resolution plan, undertaken
during covid pandemic, was a true and correct estimation of the net
value of the company? If not, can such issue be examined by this
Court under Article 142 to do complete justice inter parties?
5.  Appeal is admitted.
6.  Issue notice, returnable on 24.07.2026.
7.  Let  counter  affidavit  be  filed  by  17.07.2026.  Rejoinder
affidavit thereto, be filed by 23.07.2026.
8.  Any decision taken by NCLT shall abide by the result of the
appeal and no party shall claim any equity in respect of such
decision.
(KANCHAN CHOUHAN)                              (CHETNA BALOONI)
SENIOR PERSONAL ASSISTANT                     COURT MASTER (NSH)

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Permission to file Special Leave Petition is granted.
2. Mr. D.S. Naidu, learned senior counsel for the petitioner
submits that he is a lessee of the sugar mill and cannot be foisted

--- Page 28 ---
2
with the liability to pay election funds for conducting elections
of the Cooperative Society which is the owner of the sugar mill. He
further submitted that Cooperative Society was a defaulter and
steps were taken by a Consortium of Banks led by the Maharashtra
Cooperative Bank under SARFAESI Act and the possession of the mill
was taken over by Bank under Section 14 of SARFAESI Act and lease
was executed in favour of his client.
3. We have gone through the impugned order inter alia directing
the petitioner lessee to deposit a sum of Rs.40,11,745/- (Rs. Forty
Lakh Eleven Thousand Seven Hundred and Forty Five only) on or
before 17.06.2026 for conducting elections. Such order had been
passed on the prayer made by the Regional Joint Director (Sugar),
Pune who had been entrusted with the duty to conduct the elections
and had inter alia prayed i.e. respondent no. 2 to 4 herein (writ
petitioners in the Writ Petition) to deposit the election fund.
4. Admittedly,  Mr.  Naidu’s  client  was  not  a  party  to  the
proceeding and was not even heard before the direction came to be
passed.
5. Given these situations, we permit the petitioner to approach
the High Court within 7 days and pray for recall/modification of
the direction to deposit of a sum of Rs.40,11,745/- (Rs. Forty Lakh
Eleven Thousand Seven Hundred and Forty Five Only) by 17 th July,
2026.  Such direction shall remain stayed for a period of two weeks
to enable the petitioner to approach the High Court.
6. In the event, the petitioner fails/neglects to approach the
High Court within the time frame, the direction shall stand
automatically revived.

--- Page 29 ---
3
7. With the above directions, the Special Leave Petition is
disposed of.
8. Pending applications, if any, shall stand disposed of.

ITEM NO.27               COURT NO.5               SECTION XI-B
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Special Leave Petition (C) No(s).  21411-21420/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  11-02-2026
in CCC No. 2459/2019 11-02-2026 in CCC No. 1871/2020 11-02-2026 in
CCC No. 1820/2020 11-02-2026 in CCC No. 1855/2020 11-02-2026 in CCC
No. 1890/2020 17-03-2026 in RP No. 247/2026 17-03-2026 in RP No.
256/2026 17-03-2026 in RP No. 279/2026 17-03-2026 in RP No.
286/2026 17-03-2026 in RP No. 297/2026 passed by the High Court of
Kerala at Ernakulam]
BIJUKUMAR S                                        Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
SUKHDEEP SANGWAN SM & ORS.                         Respondent(s)
Date : 16-06-2026 These petitions were called on for hearing today.
CORAM : HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
        HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
[PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s) Mr. Raghenth Basant, Sr. Adv.
                   Mr. James P. Thomas, AOR
                   Mr. Biju P P, Adv.
                   Mr. Vinosh K K, Adv.
                                      
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Mr. Raghenth Basant, learned senior counsel for the petitioner
contends that in order dated 05.12.2023 it was unequivocally
recorded that the authorities have not complied with the order
passed on 05.06.2015 and liberty was given to comply with the said
order by re-designating the petitioner as Warrant Officer in the
pay scale fixed in Assam Rifles. He submits that the said order was
binding on a Coordinate Bench of the High Court and the latter

--- Page 31 ---
2
could not have taken a different view. He further submits that
equivalence of the petition would be with warrant officers and not
with Havildar (RL) in Assam Riffles as held in the order impugned.
2. We  have  considered  the  impugned  order  in  light  of  the
aforesaid  submission.  It  is  true  in  an  earlier  order  dated
05.12.2023, a Coordinate Bench had directed the authorities to
extend the pay scale of the Warrant Officers to the petitioner. The
matter was carried in appeal and thereafter to the Supreme Court.
The Supreme Court while dismissing the Special Leave Petition held
as follows:
“If it is the case of the petitioners that they have
already complied with the said directions, it is for
them to demonstrate the same before the learned judge.
In that context, an appeal could not have been filed
before a Division Bench of that Court.”
3. The aforesaid observations of the Supreme Court makes it clear
that  notwithstanding  dismissal  of  the  Special  Leave  Petition
against order dated 05.12.2023 a fresh opportunity was given to the
respondents  to  demonstrate  that  they  have  complied  with  the
directions of order dated 05.06.2015. The High Court rightly
appreciated  such  leave  and  came  to  be  a  finding  that  the
observations in order dated 05.12.2023 would not be held to be
conclusive and binding inter-parties. These brings us to the crux
of the matter i.e. whether re-designating the pay scale of the
petitioner on par with Havildar (RL) in Assam Rifles was in
consonance with the order dated 05.06.2015. In paragraph 10 of the
order dated 05.16.2015 it is recorded that the representation of
the petitioner before the authorities concerned was for equivalence
with Havildar (RL) and not Warrant Officer. In  light  of  such

--- Page 32 ---
3
representation and the order passed by Guwahati High Court, the
High Court had directed re-designation and replacement of the
petitioner to similar pay scales as granted in Assam Rifles.
Initially the scale of pay i.e. 3200-4900 was granted in the order
but subsequently the same was deleted. Such deletion is of no
consequence as the relief granted requires to be seen in light of
the grievance articulated by the petitioner in their representation
i.e. equivalence with the Havildar (RL). The fact that in some
other proceedings, this Court in Union of India vs. Dineshan K.K.
[(2008) 1 SCC 586] had granted equivalence with Warrant Officer is
in consequential as such persons were holding the post of Havildar
(Radio Mechanic) and the petitioner do not stand on the same
footing with them.
5. In light of these facts, we find no reason to interfere with
the impugned order passed by the High Court. Accordingly, the
Special Leave Petitions are dismissed.
6. Pending applications, if any, Shall stand disposed of.
(KANCHAN CHOUHAN)                              (CHETNA BALOONI)
SENIOR PERSONAL ASSISTANT                     COURT MASTER (NSH)

ITEM NO.31               COURT NO.5               SECTION XIV
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition(s) for Special Leave to Appeal (C)  No(s).  21330/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  16-02-2026
in WPC No. 18349/2025 passed by the High Court of Delhi at New 
Delhi]
ABHISHEK SWAMI                                     Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
COUNCIL OF SCIENTIFIC AND INDUSTRIAL RESEARCH & ORS.Respondent(s)
IA No. 174403/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED 
JUDGMENT
 
Date : 16-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM : HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
[PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s) Mr. Akash Swami, Adv.
                   Mr. Shashi Ranjan, Adv.
                   Mr. Akhilesh Tejpal, Adv.
                   Mr. Anil Kumar, AOR
                                      
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Learned counsel for the petitioner contends that clause 5(A)
of the advertisement which enables the authority to prescribe
minimum threshold marks is dehors the recruitment rules.
2. We find the recruitment rules do not expressly prohibit
fixation of minimum marks. It is one thing when the recruitment
rules expressly prohibit the fixation of minimum marks and entirely
different if they remain silent as in the present case. In the
latter situation discretion remains with the authority concerned to

--- Page 66 ---
2
fix or not to fix minimum threshold marks.
2. Clause 5(A) of the advertisement therefore, cannot be held to
run counter to the recruitment rules. The said clause is an
enabling one empowering the authority to fix minimum threshold
marks and such exercise being done prior to the examination itself
has not prejudiced the petitioner.
3. We find no reason to interfere with the impugned order passed
by the High Court. Accordingly, the Special Leave Petition is
dismissed.

ITEM NO.23               COURT NO.3               SECTION II-B
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition(s) for Special Leave to Appeal (Crl.)  No(s).  8424/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  30-01-
2026 in CRLMC No. 1623/2025 passed by the High Court of Orissa at
Cuttack]
DR. LAKSHMAN BEHERA                                Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
THE STATE OF ODISHA & ANR.                         Respondent(s)
FOR ADMISSION 
IA No. 140028/2026 - PERMISSION TO APPEAR AND ARGUE IN PERSON
 
Date : 17-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE S.V.N. BHATTI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE ATUL S. CHANDURKAR
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) :  Petitioner-in-person
                    
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard Dr.Lakshman Behera, petitioner-in-person.
2. The petitioner filed an application under Section 239 of the
Code of Criminal Procedure, 1973 (CrPC), seeking discharge
from the offences stated against him under Section 307 of the
Indian Penal Code, 1860 (IPC), read with Sections 25 and 27
of the Arms Act. 
3. The petitioner was unsuccessful before the Sessions Court in
both his prayers. The petitioner challenged the same before
the High Court of Orissa in CRLMC No.1623 of 2025. The High
Court,  through  the  impugned  order,  has  discharged  the
petitioner in so far as the offences stated against him under
Sections 25 and 27 of the Arms Act, but maintained the
offence stated against him under Section 307 IPC.

--- Page 98 ---
4. Aggrieved by this portion of the order of the High Court, the
Petitioner is before us.
5. Dr. Lakshman Behera has invited our attention to the records
and tried to convince us that, prima facie, no circumstances
were made out warranting the continuation of the trial, even
in respect of the offence stated to have been made under
Section 307 IPC. 
6. In this regard, we have taken note of the consideration of
this argument by the High Court in paragraphs 11 to 14 of the
order impugned. We are of the view that this is a matter to
be decided by the Trial Court after examining the evidence
therein, but not a case for discharge of the petitioner even
in the offence stated against him under Section 307 IPC.
7. Hence, the Special Leave Petition stands dismissed. However,
we make it clear that the Sessions Court is to proceed
uninfluenced by any of the observations made in the order
impugned before us, including the order passed by us.
8. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of.
(RASHI GUPTA)                                   (NIKITA SINGH)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)

--- Page 99 ---

                                VERSUS

Date : 18-06-2026 This appeal was called on for hearing today.
For Appellant(s) : Mr. Vishal Arun Mishra, AOR
                   
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
As per office report, certificate of service from the
concerned High Court with regard to respondent No.1 is still
awaited.   However,  Ld.  Advocate,  Mr.  Sandeep  Sharma,
appearing on behalf of Ms.Mrinal Gopal Elker, Advocate-on-
record appears for respondent No.1 and seeks time to file
vakalatnama and reply.  Vakalatnama be filed within a week.
Reply be filed within 30 days from today.
